<Review>Loved the food & ambience at Flower Child in Newport Beach @ 1302 Bison Ave.  Tonight, 3/20/21, my wife & I are celebrating my daughter's exciting achievement.

This was our first time here, so after studying the menu, we decided to start off with their avocado hummus, ordered gluten-free, with fresh vegetables to dip with, instead of the typical pita bread.  There were slender strips of red bell pepper, broccoli florets, sugar snap peas, and sliced thin carrots, yellow & white, to dunk with.  Avocado hummus was creamy & delicious and veggies were fresh & crisp.

For my main course, I ordered a Teriyaki Shrimp & Avocado Bowl, served with organic brown rice, bok choi, cauliflower, snap peas and shitaki mushrooms.  Shrimp came out fresh, hot & flavorful, and the rice & steamed veggies were tasty.  All complimented eachother.  Great dish!  I ordered a side of Yukon Gold Smashed Potatoes for $6.  This side was good, but way too much for me to finish.  I ate slightly less than half this side, before tapping out.  You could easily split this side dish.

I got a pint of Modern Times Orderville Hazy Mosaic IPA to wash it all down with.

I like how they decorated the inside of this place, as it was colorful & cheery.  We ate on their outside patio, which has tables comfortably spaced, with both overhead & stand heaters provided, plus bistro lights draped above us, to illuminate this outdoor fenced-off area.</Review>< name>
Bob Thompson</name>

<UserId.>112828455244746111861<//UserId.>< Review>
Is it worth the hype? I‚Äôll tell you one thing: it‚Äôs definitely healthier than whatever junk food you‚Äôre putting in your body, that‚Äôs for sure!

Flower Child has become quite a trend in Newport and rightfully so. If LA is known for their kale and juice diets, then Newps is similar in fashion for their organic-crazed restaurants.

This new restaurant boasts of a highly customizable menu and really caters to your dietary needs, from gluten-free to keto to vegan! I love that there‚Äôs really more than just ONE option for your dietary preference because many other places can be so restricting for those that can‚Äôt eat certain foods. With this being said, the food here isn‚Äôt exactly cheap. But you can find solace in the fact that what you‚Äôre putting into your body is organic and healthy. What could be more sinless than that?

For those that live for the kombucha hype (I most certainly do) they have an AMAZING one that is definitely worth trying.

They also have a mobile app which allows you to order it and pick up in the store or delivered wherever you are. You do also get loyalty points every time you order so it is worth downloading if you plan to come here often.

Overall, I really enjoy coming here. It isn‚Äôt someplace you‚Äôd go to daily (unless you want to seriously dent your bank account) but the food here is worth trying and the service is great.</Review>

<Review>There's a barber here named Rodney, he goes by "Hot Rod," and he happily passes out his business card saying to text him to make an appointment. I won't lie, his haircuts are nice, but his customer service skills are trash.

On Sunday, I texted him asking to book two appointments, back to back, one for me and one for my friend. He told me he doesn't work on Sundays. No problem, I replied back and said "how about tomorrow after 6 pm?" "That's cool," he says.

Based on our text messages, I wasn't completely sure that I had the appointment booked. So, on Monday, the following day, I reached out around 4:30 PM asking if after 6 would still work, and suggested booking a 6:30 and a 7:00 appointment. He hits me back with "Keep in mind I leave at 7:00. But I can stay with proper tipping etiquette." This, to me, is where all professionalism went out the window. 1.) If you leave at 7:00, and I asked for two appointments the day before for "after 6 pm," why would you not tell me you leave at 7 then? How did we go from "that's cool" to "keep in mind I leave at 7"? And why are you telling me to "Keep in mind" something that you never told me? 2.) I always tip, and I have no problem doing so, but under NO circumstances is it appropriate or professional to say "I can stay with proper tipping etiquette." Firstly, tips are optional. That's not to say I don't leave one every time, because I do, but to pressure someone into tipping with "proper etiquette" as leverage for fulfilling something you already said wouldn't be a problem the day before...seriously? Not only that, but can you imagine paying for a service anywhere else and them saying "I'm only going to serve you if you tip me properly." YOU CAN'T DO THAT. I'd love to see someone try to get away with that in a restaurant. So now, I'm uncomfortable with the pressure he's added to the whole situation, which should've been as easy as answering yes or no, and I calmly explain why.  I tell him that if he's happy to schedule my friend and I for 6:30 and 7:00 then I'll see him then, "if not, I'll just schedule for a different day. But the pressure just doesn't make me feel very welcome. Hope you understand."

He then replies back at 6:43, basically 15 minutes AFTER the first appointment would have started, saying "yes your right I feel pressured has well. People making demands about waiting without building a relationship first. Or seeing how I run my business. Don't think this is good energy to move forward with. Thanks for reaching out, sorry it didn't work." [all those typos are his by the way, not mine.]

To clarify, I never made demands about not having to wait. I requested an appointment, and he demanded that I have "proper tipping etiquette" because him leaving at 7, when he never told me that, suddenly became my issue. He also said we haven't built a relationship and I don't know how he runs his business when I've already seen him three times before. He clearly didn't even know who he was talking to, and he clearly didn't care. So now, after adding undue pressure to scheduling an appointment, something that should be simple and painless, he essentially says I shouldn't be his customer anymore. Because he demanded "proper tipping etiquette," he missed out on my $30 to pay for the service + my tip, and my friends $30 service + tip, as well as all the future $30 haircuts + tip I would've paid for in the future. I'm shocked by his diva attitude and general unpleasantness to his customers. If you're looking to be treated like a regular customer, who regularly pays and tips their barber, don't go here, and definitely don't see "Hot Rod". You'll be treated like second class trash. That is inexcusable.</Review>< Pictures>

<Name>John Garcii</Name><time>1546899103593</time><rate>5</rate><text>The Golden Deli is one of the best Vietnamese Restaurants I have ever been to in my life. I have been eating Vietnamese food for 5 years not and I know what is expected and not expected. The atmosphere is very fast and going - you know when you're in there that people are eating crazy fast and they are going in and out. Like the atmosphere, the service is almost scary fast, I was wish a group of three and we ordered 10-12 items, ranging from food to drinks, and they all arrived in under 15 minutes. With there being over 40 people on such a small area you would be surprised at how fast they were. The food was fantastic! The flavor was very good, not over done, or too much seasoning, the Vietnamese coffee was just a heart attack in the waiting. The price and wait times are last but not least. The wait times can go from 15-50 minutes depending on the volume of customers. And the price is dirt cheap. You will never find a mix of high quality and low prices for this quick of service anywhere else in the Valley.<//text><pics>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNHZnMX29EPZfG0Ys7iNt5U_ghF85eF_fAfMyBq=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOCuxrUwFNIP4P1K_Mr5upgOl2hsNEse44OKbPh=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipMUyaNkJRyT1jMXHNVA7FscClrOYXnMBnaaB_ie=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPeV0xZjB_mDoz-7OZK0iZZLH3Np796YQt-PvC7=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipMC6fjnQAXWaMkOBsTar7ZcDFlStvN3KBYsYd3n=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOYwMZ8oQusSnh4eJfUMh_tagsoXkq-nG0MrRX1=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipMG_dia-ikDxmOOcq0T_VpXso0jRNozWwd5rpBK=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]<//pics><Response>None</Response><Gmap_id>0x80c2db2ac87d1897:0xd50fbd33a3056663< /Gmap_id></record>

Vincent Hoey< /Name>
< Text>
Pretty popular Vietnamese restaurant in San Gabriel that has an extensive menu to satisfy any cravings. I came based on my friend's recommendation that their imperial rolls are elite so I definitely had to give it a try.

They're usually pretty busy on the weekends with a wait but I came on a Saturday morning and was seated immediately. It's in a small plaza with a lot so parking wasn't that bad.

Their menu is pretty much the Bible of Vietnamese cuisine - it had a little bit of everything from pho to vermicelli to broken rice plates. I went with their bun thit nuong & cha gio (vermicelli with grilled pork and imperial rolls). It was average at best and will just get the job done.

Overall I thought it was okay, nothing too "WOW" or made my taste buds jump. The imperial rolls were definitely good and had a nice crunch to them, but I personally believe there are better options out there for Vietnamese food.</Text>

<Rate>5< /Rate><Review>It is safe to say that Golden Deli is the most authentic and delicious Vietnamese food I have ever had the pleasure of trying.

Came here with a few buddies on a Saturday around 3pm and was able to be seated after 10-15 minutes.  If you wait until later, expect to wait in long lines.

Once you sit down, they tend to you immediately and they‚Äôll keep checking on you at least 5-10 times throughout your meal which I appreciate in a busy place like this where you constantly want to add more and more to your order and refill your drinks!

We went all out and started with a few appetizers of egg rolls, multiple bowls of pho, and dinner plate entrees.

The egg rolls are different than any I‚Äôve had prior.  They are giant rolls that are blistered on the outside to keep it super crispy on the outside, but soft and flavorful on the inside.  They are so addicting we had 3 orders of them.   It is highly recommended that you wrap with mint leaves and the lettuce they give you and dip it in your small bowl of broth with carrots.  You will NOT be disappointed if you do so!

The shrimp paste had me hesitant because of the word ‚Äúpaste‚Äù but it is nothing like that. The best way I can describe is is ground shrimp cooked in oil and formed to perfection.

The #89B dinner plate was just as fantastic.  It comes with egg rolls, shrimp paste, and grilled beef.  Lots of good flavor, highly recommend adding some of the side sauces they provide at the table to fit your liking.

The Pho we had was the icing on the cake.  I enjoy having a nice broth or a soup at the end of a meal to ‚Äúfill the cracks‚Äù lol.  The broth was extremely flavorful and not too salty and the meat was tender and delicious.  Add chili oil to it as you please if you like a little more kick.

I have absolutely no complaints when it comes to this spot.  I highly recommend to anyone who loves or wants to try authentic Vietnamese food!<//Review>< Pics>

< Review>
Yummy weekend breakfast. No wait, quick and delicious food! They brought out hot tea which was nice.

I got pho with brisket and steak. The broth was soothing and the flavors were well balanced. The beef was so tender too!

My husband got the chicken curry noodle which he enjoyed. He always substitutes the vermicelli with egg noodle instead which goes well with the curry and holds up better to the thicker broth.

We'll be back! The egg rolls looked really good and I'd like to try it next time! They come with 5 so we thought it'd be too much food for us.< /Review>

Just revisited my childhood favorite Pho place during the pandemic, and my wife and I were thoroughly disappointed! Pretty good food with decent prices here.  I like that they have a decent variety of Vietnamese food here.  The major cons are that they are ALWAYS busy and the parking situation is hell. <Gmap_id>0x80c2db2ac87d1897:0xd50fbd33a3056663<//Gmap_id>< Review>
Ever since reading Jonathan Gold's LA Weekly article about this noodle shop, I knew I had to try it, especially since I'm from San Gabriel Valley (Arcadia to be specific).  I used to indulge in pho every once in awhile.  However, this place has utterly ruined me.

The difference lies in the broth.  There's something inexplicably subtle & exquisite about the broth.  I'm not Vietnamese nor do I pretend to be the utmost authority on pho but I would drive from West Hollywood to San Gabriel just for Golden Deli's pho.  That's how good it is.  I always get the beef balls (the Vietnamese version of Italian meatballs) in noodle soup.  I'm sure the other noodle soups are on par as well.< /Review>

<Text>You'll be hard pressed to find another Vietnamese place as recognizable as Golden Deli (and with good reason). The restaurant is located on a corner plaza and parking may be difficult during peak hours. And yet the line to get a table may be even longer. Avoid busy hours if you don't want to wait an exorbitant amount of time.

The menu puts cheesecake factory's menu to shame with the amount of food there is. My boyfriend and I like to stick with the basics: ph√≥ of any variety, spring rolls, egg rolls, beef stew, c√≥m t√°m (broken rice), iced coffee, and soda chanh. The flavors are really simple but executed to near perfection. I have yet to taste a ph√≥ broth as good as the one they serve here. They pack a good amount of meat and rice for the c√≥m t√°m dishes. The beef stew (b√≤ kho) is a favorite of the boyfriend. The broth is more soupy than its western counterparts, but it packs the same amount of flavor without the accompanying heaviness of a western beef stew.

The prices are extremely fair and something I'd call a steal. You'll spend less than $30 for a couple's dinner (appetizer, drinks included).<//Text><gmapID>0x80c2db2ac87d1897:0xd50fbd33a3056663</gmapID>< name>

<user_name>Matt Kelley<//user_name></record></dataset><record>
<userid>110704716013971109471</userid><Rating>3<//Rating><review>Golden Deli sits anonymously in a strip mall amidst several other eateries, from the outside completely unassuming. Open the door to Golden Deli and BAM, hustle and bustle, noise and an extremely active dining room. Now, mind you, if you enter any decent eating establishment in the middle of a dinner or lunch rush, this is to be expected. HOWEVER, I stepped into Golden Deli at around 2:30, a fair amount of time after the lunch rush. I love a dining room alive with the din of servers and customers enjoying a meal, it's as intoxicating as any part of the dining experience.

As soon as I entered the dining room, I was IMMEDIATELY greeted (possibly a bit too aggressively for some), informing the server that I was ordering something to go and she handed me a menu. I had already perused through the menu prior to my arrival, so I already had an idea what I was ordering. It was a scorcher of a day in Southern California, approaching triple digits, so seemingly one of Golden Deli's specialties, a soup or stew, just wasn't an option. I also needed something quick and easy so decided to go with a banh mi, a Vietnamese sandwich. I ordered my sandwich with shredded pork (meat and skin), the banh mi bi. The banh mi came as expected with cilantro, pickled carrots & daikon, cucumber, jalapenos, and a spicy chili sauce. The sandwich was....okay. The shredded pork had a grainy texture to it and the sauce had very little heat. Everything else was adequate and the baguette was properly crusty.

On another day and maybe a large bowl of pho, my overall experience might have been different, but on this occasion, I loved the hectic vibe, but the food left me unimpressed.<//review><Date>1406356006937<//Date><pictures>None</pictures><gmap_id>0x80c2db2ac87d1897:0xd50fbd33a3056663< /gmap_id><Response>None< /Response>< name>
Russell Saisho</name>
</record></dataset><record>

<Time>1406356006937<//Time><pics>None< /pics><review>Golden Deli sits anonymously in a strip mall amidst several other eateries, from the outside completely unassuming. Open the door to Golden Deli and BAM, hustle and bustle, noise and an extremely active dining room. Now, mind you, if you enter any decent eating establishment in the middle of a dinner or lunch rush, this is to be expected. HOWEVER, I stepped into Golden Deli at around 2:30, a fair amount of time after the lunch rush. I love a dining room alive with the din of servers and customers enjoying a meal, it's as intoxicating as any part of the dining experience.

As soon as I entered the dining room, I was IMMEDIATELY greeted (possibly a bit too aggressively for some), informing the server that I was ordering something to go and she handed me a menu. I had already perused through the menu prior to my arrival, so I already had an idea what I was ordering. It was a scorcher of a day in Southern California, approaching triple digits, so seemingly one of Golden Deli's specialties, a soup or stew, just wasn't an option. I also needed something quick and easy so decided to go with a banh mi, a Vietnamese sandwich. I ordered my sandwich with shredded pork (meat and skin), the banh mi bi. The banh mi came as expected with cilantro, pickled carrots & daikon, cucumber, jalapenos, and a spicy chili sauce. The sandwich was....okay. The shredded pork had a grainy texture to it and the sauce had very little heat. Everything else was adequate and the baguette was properly crusty.

On another day and maybe a large bowl of pho, my overall experience might have been different, but on this occasion, I loved the hectic vibe, but the food left me unimpressed.<//review><Response>None</Response><name>Russell Saisho<//name></record>

<rating>3< /rating>< Review>
This place is popular. It's a weekday lunch and there's a 10 minute wait. My background in Pho is that I'm spoiled, Little Saigon Westminster spoiled. Parking in the lot sucks. You almost need to stalk someone to get a spot here. There is a neighborhood street around the side where I ended up parking my car, but you don't always want to rely on that.

-=-#1 Pho-=- At almost every Pho place I've been to, hundreds maybe thousands (ok that's exaggerating), the #1 is the largest serving of Pho with all the meats including all the rare cuts, well done cuts, and tendons. One thing that was a bit different here was that some of the meat was cut in cubes, rather than your typical slices. Who notices that really.. just me the seasoned Pho eater.

-=-Spring Roll-=-It's a spring roll. It's really hard to mess up as long as you get the contents right. So now it's down to the sauce. It's average. Good, not the sweetest and tangiest, but it's between the 50th and 60th percentile of what I've had before.</Review>
